                  <section class="section bg-dark-blue">
    <div class="section__wrapper">
      <h1 class="legal-page__heading">
        Sample list of higher risk IP addresses
      </h1>
    </div>
  </section>

  <section class="section">
    <div class="section__wrapper text-dark-blue">
      <p>
        This list includes IP addresses that are associated with risk signals
        based on the
        <a href="/en/solutions/fraud-prevention/overview"
          >minFraud network</a
        >. These IPs are often linked to suspicious behavior, such as
        anonymizing services, bot activity, or patterns commonly associated with
        fraud.
      </p>

      <p>
        While this sample may be useful for testing or research purposes, it
        reflects only a tiny fraction of the IPs flagged by minFraud. Risk can
        also depend on context. The same IP might appear low-risk in one
        scenario and high-risk in another.
      </p>

      <p>The list is updated twice monthly.</p>

      <p>
        If you're evaluating IP risk as part of your fraud prevention strategy,
        the
        <a href="/en/solutions/fraud-prevention/plans-pricing">minFraud Score</a>
        provides a more complete picture. It considers a wide range of factors,
        including IP reputation, device traits, and behavioral signals, to
        deliver a real-time risk assessment.
      </p>

      <p>
        To identify anonymous IP addresses in support of geotargeting and ad
        serving environments, we recommend using the
        <a href="/en/geoip-anonymous-ip-database"
          >GeoIP Anonymous</a
        >
        or
        <a href="/en/geoip-anonymous-plus-database"
          >Anonymous Plus</a
        >
        databases.
      </p>
